B0076I8O70|5.0|The original lineip of It Bites...Francis Dunnery (guitars, vocals), John Beck (keyboards, backing & harmony vocals) Dick Nolan (bass, backing vocals) and Bob Dalton (drums, backing vocals) produced three solid, hook-filled, tuneful, guitar-crunchy prog rock albums between 1986 and 1989: [[ASIN:B000024XCW The Big Lad in the Windmill]], [[ASIN:B00009P8NU Once Around the World]], and [[ASIN:B00008LLC4 Eat Me in St. Louis]]. Frontman Francis Dunnery had a voice not unlike Genesis-era Peter Gabriel, although the band was certainly not a Genesis clone. They rocked a little harder, had a little more attitude, and were not as rigidly tied to old-school prog as some of their contemporaries. They were a rock band with prog overtones, and they rocked indeed.<br /><br />Dunnery left in 1990 to pursue a solo career. The remaining members shifted around a bit, sometimes under the It Bites banner, other times with a new name (such as the pairing of Beck and Daltion with John Mitchell (from Arena and Frost*, lead vocals and guitars) and Pete Trewavas (from Marillion, bass) as \\"Kino.\\" The lineup released the well-received [[ASIN:B00079RNKE Picture]] in 2005.<br /><br />In 2006, the nucleus of Beck, Dalton and Mitchell became the new It Bites and in 2008 released the critically acclaimed [[ASIN:B001F0PR52 Tall Ships]]. The band hadn't successfully \\"replaced\\" Dunnery...those were some big and distinctive shoes to fill...as much as found a way to carry on in the spirit of the band's original vibe.<br /><br />Fast-forward to the present...2012...and the new album, \\"Map of the Past.\\" Founding member Dick Nolan is gone, replaced by Lee Pomeroy. Other than that, the momentum established by Dalton, Mitchell and Beck on \\"The Tall Ships\\" continues with what many consider to be a superior follow-up to an already classic first post-Dunnery effort.<br /><br />It's unfortunate that in the United States, this album has flown completely under the radar. As you can see from this review, it's available here only as an import, and it's received virtually no fanfare. But if you venture \\"across the pond\\" to the Amazon U.K. Website, you'll see a large group of enthusiastic reviewers who have awarded this four and five stars.<br /><br />11 songs, 52 minutes, and in the tradition of classic It Bites, most tracks clock in at 4 minutes while two of them stretch out to 6.<br /><br />Like many bands who arrived in the second wave of prog following Yes, Genesis, Kin Crimson et. al., you could spend all day listening to these tracks while playing \\"spot the influence.\\" The opener, \\"Man In The Photograph,\\" is a slowly-building, keyboard-driven ballad in the Procol Harum mold. That segues into the guitar-driven, riff-happy stomper \\"Wallflower,\\" which really harkens back to the Dunnery era (as well as Mitchell's work in Frost*). \\"Cartoon Graveyard\\" is another track that leans heavily on the classic It Bites sound. \\"Meadow and the Stream\\" has \\"big prog epic\\" written all over it, reminiscent of the title track to the Frost* album [[ASIN:B000G04UYG Milliontown]] while throwing in several heaping measures of \\"Lamb\\"-era Genesis. \\"The Last Escape\\" is a nice moody, tuneful, atmospheric track with tasty guitar solos, and it feels like a suitable closer for the album...although that distinction goes to \\"Exit Song, clocking in at a minute and a half, performed by Mitchell on acoustic guitar.<br /><br />I have mixed feelings about the band if I listen to the new material and follow it with a listent to any of the Dunnery tracks. As an example, in my copy of iTunes, \\"Map of the Past\\" is immediately followed by the blast of \\"Once Around The World\\" and the signature Dunnery tune, \\"Midnight.\\" It's in that moment that I realize comparisons to the old and new are futile here...Mitchell's not Dunnery, nor should he attempt to be...so in the same way that it's possible to enjoy [[ASIN:B000002J1M Foxtrot]] and [[ASIN:B000002J2B Wind & Wuthering]] as two fine efforts by different editions of thesame band, \\"Map of the Past\\" should also be enjoyed.<br /><br />A nice visit from old friends whose musical future remains bright.

They both need serious therapy. There is absolutely nothing sexy or loving with this couple.<br /><br />The sex is continual and let's face it, quite boring. The author repeats herself continually - from comments, to descriptors, to blah blah blah there is just nothing exciting here.<br />I could easily go on and on but as I said, I don't want this to become a tirade, and frankly this book isn't worth my time.<br /><br />Save your money folks and find something else.
